transliteration"><span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Cantonese" title="Help:IPA/Cantonese">[l&#596;&#768;&#720;k&#794;.j&#339;&#783;&#720;&#331;]</a></span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a></th><td><span lang="yue-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Yue Chinese-language transliteration">Lok<sup>6</sup>-joeng<sup>4</sup></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcffc9;"><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Romanization_System" title="Taiwanese Romanization System">T&#226;i-l&#244;</a></th><td><span lang="nan-Latn" style="font-style:normal" title="Taiwanese Hokkien-language transliteration">Lo&#781;k-i&#244;ng</span></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div></div>\n<p><b>Luoyang</b> (<i lang="zh-Latn" title="Chinese-language transliteration">Lu&#242;y&#225;ng</i>)  is a city located in the confluence area of <a href="/wiki/Luo_River_(Henan)" title="Luo River (Henan)">Luo River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a> in the west of <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> province. Governed as a <a href="/wiki/Prefecture-level_city" title="Prefecture-level city">prefecture-level city</a>, it borders the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Zhengzhou" title="Zhengzhou">Zhengzhou</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Pingdingshan" title="Pingdingshan">Pingdingshan</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Nanyang,_Henan" title="Nanyang, Henan">Nanyang</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Sanmenxia" title="Sanmenxia">Sanmenxia</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Jiyuan" title="Jiyuan">Jiyuan</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/Jiaozuo" title="Jiaozuo">Jiaozuo</a> to the northeast. As of the final 2010 census, Luoyang had a population of 6,549,941 inhabitants with 1,857,003 people living in the built-up (<i>or metro</i>) area made of the city\'s five urban districts, all of which except the <a href="/wiki/Jili_District" title="Jili District">Jili District</a> are not urbanized yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Situated on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Plain_(China)" title="Central Plain (China)">central plain</a> of China, Luoyang is one of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_China#Ancient_China" title="History of China">cradles of Chinese civilization</a>, and is one of the <a href="/wiki/Historical_capitals_of_China" title="Historical capitals of China">Four Great Ancient Capitals of China</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Names"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Names</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#World_Heritage"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">World Heritage</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Ancient_city_sites"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Ancient city sites</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Transportation"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transportation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Twin_towns_and_sister_cities"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Twin towns and sister cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Famous_residents"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Famous residents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name "Luoyang" originates from the city\'s location on the north or sunny (<a href="/wiki/Yin_and_yang#Toponymy" title="Yin and yang">"yang"</a>) side of the <a href="/wiki/Luo_River_(Henan)" title="Luo River (Henan)">Luo River</a>. Since the river flows from west to east and the sun is to the south of the river, the sun always shines on the north side of the river. Luoyang has had several names over the centuries, including "Luoyi" (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27931;&#37009;</span>) and "Luozhou (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27931;&#24030;</span>)", though Luoyang has been its primary name. It has been called, during various periods, "Dongdu" (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#19996;&#37117;</span>, meaning the Eastern Capital, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a>), "Xijing" (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#35199;&#20140;</span>, meaning the Western Capital, during the Song Dynasty), or "Jingluo" (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#20140;&#27931;</span>, meaning the general capital for China). During the rule of <a href="/wiki/Wu_Zetian" title="Wu Zetian">Wu Zetian</a>, the city was known as Shendu (&#31070;&#37117; divine capital)\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:263px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg/261px-Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg/392px-Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg/522px-Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg 2x" width="261"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Longmen_Grottoes_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Longmen_Grottoes" title="Longmen Grottoes">Longmen Grottoes</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:263px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg/261px-%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg/392px-%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg/522px-%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg 2x" width="261"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A9%E5%AD%90%E9%A9%BE%E5%85%AD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Museum of Luoyang Eastern Zhou Royal Horse and Chariot Pits</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="395" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif/280px-Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif/420px-Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luoyang_in_Han_Dynasty.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Luoyang in Eastern Han Dynasty when it was the capital of China</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:287px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="1040" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg/285px-China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg/428px-China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg/570px-China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg 2x" width="285"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:China-henan-luoyang-white-horse-temple-entrance-20040506.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/White_Horse_Temple" title="White Horse Temple">White Horse Temple</a> gate</div></div></div>\n<p>The greater Luoyang area has been sacred ground since the late <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic period</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This area at the intersection of the <a href="/wiki/Luo_River_(Henan)" title="Luo River (Henan)">Luo river</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_River_(China)" title="Yi River (China)">Yi River</a> was considered to be the geographical center of China.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Because of this sacred aspect, several cities &#8211; all of which are generally referred to as "Luoyang" &#8211; have been built in this area. In 2070&#160;BC, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xia_Dynasty" title="Xia Dynasty">Xia Dynasty</a> king <a href="/wiki/Tai_Kang" title="Tai Kang">Tai Kang</a> moved the Xia capital to the intersection of the Luo and Yi and named the city <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erlitou" title="Erlitou">Zhenxun</a> (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#26015;&#37161;</span>). In 1600&#160;BC, <a href="/wiki/Tang_of_Shang" title="Tang of Shang">Tang of Shang</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Jie_of_Xia" title="Jie of Xia">Jie</a>, the final Xia Dynasty king, and built Western Bo (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#35199;&#20147;</span>), a new capital on the Luo River. The ruins of Western Bo are located in Luoyang Prefecture.\n</p><p>In the 1036&#160;BC a settlement named Chengzhou (<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#25104;&#21608;</span>) was constructed by the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Zhou" title="Duke of Zhou">Duke of Zhou</a> for the remnants of the captured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shang_Dynasty" title="Shang Dynasty">Shang</a> nobility. The Duke also moved the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Tripod_Cauldrons" title="Nine Tripod Cauldrons">Nine Tripod Cauldrons</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chengzhou" title="Chengzhou">Chengzhou</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhou_Dynasty" title="Zhou Dynasty">Zhou Dynasty</a> capital at <a href="/wiki/Haojing" title="Haojing">Haojing</a>. A second Western Zhou capital, <a href="/wiki/Wangcheng_(Zhou_dynasty)" title="Wangcheng (Zhou dynasty)">Wangcheng</a> (also: Luoyi) was built 15&#160;km (9.3&#160;mi) west of Chengzhou.  Wangcheng became the capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Zhou_Dynasty" title="Eastern Zhou Dynasty">Eastern Zhou Dynasty</a> in 771&#160;BC.  The Eastern Zhou Dynasty capital was moved to Chengzhou in 510&#160;BC. Later, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Han_Dynasty" title="Eastern Han Dynasty">Eastern Han Dynasty</a> capital of Luoyang would be built over Chengzhou.  Modern Luoyang is built over the ruins of Wangcheng, which are still visible today at Wangcheng Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 25 AD, Luoyang was declared the capital of the Eastern Han Dynasty on November 27 by <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Guangwu_of_Han" title="Emperor Guangwu of Han">Emperor Guangwu of Han</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hymes_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hymes-3">[3]</a></sup> For several centuries, Luoyang was the focal point of China. In AD 68, the <a href="/wiki/White_Horse_Temple" title="White Horse Temple">White Horse Temple</a>, the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> temple in China, was founded in Luoyang. The temple still exists, though the architecture is of later origin, mainly from the 16th century. <a href="/wiki/An_Shigao" title="An Shigao">An Shigao</a> was one of the first monks to popularize Buddhism in Luoyang.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ban_Chao" title="Ban Chao">ambassador Banchao</a> restored the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> in Eastern Han Dynasty and this has made the capital city Luoyang the start of Silk Road\n</p><p>In 166 AD, the first <a href="/wiki/Sino-Roman_relations" title="Sino-Roman relations">Roman mission</a>, sent by "the king of Da Qin [the Roman Empire], Andun" (<a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius Antoninus</a>, r. 161&#8211;180 AD), reached Luoyang after arriving by sea in Rinan Commandery in what is now central <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The late 2nd century saw China decline into anarchy:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>The decline was accelerated by the rebellion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_Turbans" title="Yellow Turbans">Yellow Turbans</a>, who, although defeated by the Imperial troops in 184 AD, weakened the state to the point where there was a continuing series of rebellions degenerating into civil war, culminating in the burning of the Han capital of Luoyang on 24 September 189 AD. This was followed by a state of continual unrest and wars in China until a modicum of stability returned in the 220s, but with the establishment of three separate kingdoms, rather than a unified empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>In 190 AD, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Dong_Zhuo" title="Dong Zhuo">Dong Zhuo</a> ordered his soldiers to ransack, pillage, and raze the city as he retreated from <a href="/wiki/Campaign_against_Dong_Zhuo" title="Campaign against Dong Zhuo">the coalition set up against him</a> by regional lords all across China. The court was subsequently moved to the more defensible western city of <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a>. Following a period of disorder, during which warlord <a href="/wiki/Cao_Cao" title="Cao Cao">Cao Cao</a> held the last Han emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Xiandi" title="Han Xiandi">Xian</a> in <a href="/wiki/Xuchang" title="Xuchang">Xuchang</a> (196&#8211;220), Luoyang was restored to prominence when his son Cao Pi, <a href="/wiki/Cao_Pi" title="Cao Pi">Emperor Wen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Cao_Wei" title="Cao Wei">Wei Dynasty</a>, declared it his capital in 220 AD. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jin_Dynasty_(265%E2%80%93420)" title="Jin Dynasty (265&#8211;420)">Jin Dynasty</a>, successor to Wei, was also established in Luoyang.\n</p><p>When Jin was overrun by <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> forces in 311 AD, it was forced to move its capital to <a href="/wiki/Jiankang" title="Jiankang">Jiankang</a> (modern day <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a>). The Xiongnu warriors then sacked and nearly totally destroyed Luoyang. The same fate befell <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an" title="Chang\'an">Chang\'an</a> in 316 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rene_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rene-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In winter 416, Luoyang fell to <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Liu_Song" title="Emperor Wu of Liu Song">Liu Yu</a>\'s general <a href="/wiki/Tan_Daoji" title="Tan Daoji">Tan Daoji</a>. In 422, Luoyang was captured by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Wei" title="Northern Wei">Northern Wei</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liu_Song" title="Liu Song">Liu Song</a> general Dao Yanzhi took the city back, but by 439 the Wei conquered the city definitively. In 493 AD, <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Xiaowen_of_Northern_Wei" title="Emperor Xiaowen of Northern Wei">Emperor Xiaowen</a> of the Northern Wei dynasty moved the capital from <a href="/wiki/Datong" title="Datong">Datong</a> to Luoyang and started the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Rock-cut_architecture" title="Rock-cut architecture">rock-cut</a> <a href="/wiki/Longmen_Grottoes" title="Longmen Grottoes">Longmen Grottoes</a>. More than 30,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> statues from the time of this dynasty have been found in the caves. Many of these sculptures were two-faced. At the same time, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaolin_Temple" title="Shaolin Temple">Shaolin Temple</a> was also built by the Emperor to accommodate an Indian monk on the Mont Song right next to Luoyang City. The <a href="/wiki/Yongning_Pagoda" title="Yongning Pagoda">Yongning Temple</a> (<span lang="zh-Hans" title="Chinese language text">&#27704;&#23425;&#23546;</span>), the tallest pagoda in China, was also built in Luoyang.\n</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Yang_of_Sui" title="Emperor Yang of Sui">Emperor Yang of Sui</a> took control in 604 AD he founded the new Luoyang on the site of the existing city using a layout inspired by his father <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wen_of_Sui" title="Emperor Wen of Sui">Emperor Wen of Sui</a>\'s work in newly rebuilt Chang\'an.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tang_Dynasty" title="Tang Dynasty">Tang Dynasty</a>, Luoyang was Dongdu (<span lang="zh-Hant" title="Chinese language text">&#19996;&#37117;</span>), the "Eastern Capital", and at its height had a population of around one million, second only to Chang\'an, which, at the time, was the largest city in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the interval of Tang Dynasty, the first and the only empress in Chinese history &#8211; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empress_Wu" title="Empress Wu">Empress Wu</a>, moved the capital of her Zhou Dynasty to Luoyang and named it as Shen Du (Capital of the God). She constructed the tallest palace in Chinese history, which is now in the site of Sui Tang Luoyang city.\n</p><p>During the short-lived Five Dynasties, Luoyang was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Later_Liang_(Five_Dynasties)" title="Later Liang (Five Dynasties)">Later Liang</a> (only for a few years before the court moved to <a href="/wiki/Kaifeng" title="Kaifeng">Kaifeng</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Later_Tang" title="Later Tang">Later Tang</a>.\n</p><p>During the North <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_Dynasty" title="Song Dynasty">Song Dynasty</a>, Luoyang was the \'Western Capital\' and birthplace of Zhao Kuangyin, the founder of the Song Dynasty. It served as a prominent culture center, housing some of the most important philosophers.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Jin_dynasty_(1115%E2%80%931234)" title="Jin dynasty (1115&#8211;1234)">Jin Dynasty</a>, Luoyang was the "Middle Capital".\n</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a>, Luoyang was no longer the capital of China in the rest of the ancient dynasties. The population was reduced to that of an average county. However, for one last time, Luoyang city was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> for a brief period of time during the Japanese invasion. By 1949, Luoyang\'s population was 75,000.\n</p><p>After the People\'s Republic of China was established, Luoyang was revived as a major heavy industrial hub. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_five-year_plan_(China)" title="First five-year plan (China)">first five-year plan of China</a>, 7 of 156 Soviet-aided major industrial programmes was launched in Luoyang\'s <a href="/wiki/Jianxi_District" title="Jianxi District">Jianxi District</a>, including Dongfanghong Tractor Factory, Luoyang Mining Machines Factory and Luoyang Bearing Factory. Later, during the <a href="/wiki/Third_Front_(China)" title="Third Front (China)">Third Front</a> construction, a group of heavy industry factories was moved to or founded in Luoyang, including Luoyang Glass Factory. Industrial development significantly shifted Luoyang\'s demographic makeup, and about half of Luoyang\'s population are new immigrants after 1949 from outside the province or their descendants.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage">World Heritage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: World Heritage">edit</a><span &#8211; Han Wei Luoyang City Site, Dingding Gate Site of Sui Tang Luoyang City, Xin\'an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanguguan" title="Hanguguan">Hangu Guan</a> Site (2014.6.22)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_city_sites">Ancient city sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span held a population of 1,857,003, making it the fourth-largest city in <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a>. The entire area of Luoyang&#8217;s municipal government held 6,549,941 inhabitants total.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Map\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><div class="center" style="position: relative">\n<div class="noresize" role="img" style="width: 575px; Jili</b></a></div>\n</div>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As <a href="#Names">its name states</a>, the Old Town of Luoyang is located on the north bank of the <a href="/wiki/Luo_River_(Henan)" title="Luo River (Henan)">Luo</a>, a southern tributary of the middle reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_River" title="Yellow River">Yellow River</a>. The districts of the modern urban center include both banks and some of the surrounding mountains.\n</p><p>The countryside controlled by the municipal government includes still more rugged land: mountains comprise 45.51% of the total area; hills, 40.73%; and plains, 13.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:230px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guanlin_Templ.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="584" data-file-width="778" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Guanlin_Templ.JPG/228px-Guanlin_Templ.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Guanlin_Templ.JPG/342px-Guanlin_Templ.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/be/Guanlin_Templ.JPG/456px-Guanlin_Templ.JPG 2x" width="228"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guanlin_Templ.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guanlin_Temple&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guanlin Temple (page does not exist)">Guanlin Temple</a> in May 2007.</div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>Sites</dt></dl>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Longmen_Grottoes" title="Longmen Grottoes">Longmen Grottoes</a> south of the city were listed on the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> list of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> in November 2000. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guanlin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guanlin (page does not exist)">Guanlin</a>&#8212;a series of temples built in honor of <a href="/wiki/Guan_Yu" title="Guan Yu">Guan Yu</a>, a hero of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms_period" title="Three Kingdoms period">Three Kingdoms period</a>&#8212;is nearby. The <a href="/wiki/White_Horse_Temple" title="White Horse Temple">White Horse Temple</a> is located 12&#160;km (7.5&#160;mi) east of the modern town.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Luoyang_Museum" title="Luoyang Museum">Luoyang Museum</a> (est.&#8201;1958) features ancient relics dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Xia_dynasty" title="Xia dynasty">Xia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shang_Dynasty" title="Shang Dynasty">Shang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zhou_dynasty" title="Zhou dynasty">Zhou</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_dynasties" title="List of Chinese dynasties">dynasties</a>. The total number of exhibits on display is 1,700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> China\'s only tomb museum, the <a href="/wiki/Luoyang_Ancient_Tombs_Museum" title="Luoyang Ancient Tombs Museum">Luoyang Ancient Tombs Museum</a>, opened to the public in 1987 and is situated north of the modern town.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gaocheng_Astronomical_Observatory" title="Gaocheng Astronomical Observatory">Gaocheng Astronomical Observatory</a> (also known as the Dengfeng Observatory or the Tower of Chou Kong) stands 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) south-east of Luoyang. It was constructed in 1276 during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty" title="Yuan Dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a> by <a href="/wiki/Guo_Shoujing" title="Guo Shoujing">Guo Shoujing</a> as a giant <a href="/wiki/Gnomon" title="Gnomon">gnomon</a> for "the measurement of the sun\'s shadow". Prior to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit_China_Missions" title="Jesuit China Missions">Jesuit China Missions</a>, it was used for establishing the <a href="/wiki/Summer_solstice" title="Summer solstice">summer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winter_solstice" title="Winter solstice">winter solstices</a> in traditional <a href="/wiki/Chinese_astronomy" title="Chinese astronomy">Chinese astronomy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Cuisine</dt></dl>\n<p>Luoyang is famed for its <a href="/wiki/Water_Banquet" title="Water Banquet">Water Banquet</a>, which consists of 8 cold and 16 warm dishes all cooked in various broths, gravies, or juices.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Botany</dt></dl>\n<p>Luoyang is also celebrated for the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Paeonia_suffruticosa" title="Paeonia suffruticosa">peonies</a>, its city flower. Since 1983, each mid-April the city hosts the Peony Culture Festival of Luoyang China. More than 19 million tourists visited Luoyang during the 2014 festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Music</dt></dl>\n<p>"Spring in Luoyang" (<span class="nowrap"><span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%B4%9B%E9%98%B3" title="wikt:&#27931;&#38451;">&#27931;&#38451;</a><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E6%98%A5" title="wikt:&#26149;">&#26149;</a></span></span>, <i>Lu&#242;y&#225;ng Ch&#363;n</i>), an ancient Chinese composition, became popular in <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo dynasty</a> (918&#8211;1392) and is still performed in its <i><a href="/wiki/Dangak" title="Dangak">dangak</a></i> (Koreanized) version <i>Nakyangchun</i> <span class="nowrap">(<span lang="ko" title="Korean language text">&#45209;&#50577;&#52632;</span>).</span> <a href="/wiki/Lou_Harrison" title="Lou Harrison">Lou Harrison</a>, an American composer, has also created an arrangement of the work.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Dialect</dt></dl>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Luoyang_dialect" title="Luoyang dialect">Luoyang dialect</a></div>\n<p>Residents of Luoyang typically speak a dialect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhongyuan_Mandarin" title="Zhongyuan Mandarin">Zhongyuan Mandarin</a>. Although Luoyang\'s dialect was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prestige_dialect" title="Prestige dialect">prestige dialect</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dialects_of_Chinese" title="Dialects of Chinese">spoken Chinese</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Warring_States_period" title="Warring States period">Warring States period</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Zhou_dynasty" title="Eastern Zhou dynasty">Zhou</a> until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ming_Dynasty" title="Ming Dynasty">Ming Dynasty</a>, it differs from the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_dialect" title="Beijing dialect">Beijing form</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandarin_dialects" title="Mandarin dialects">Mandarin</a> which became the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chinese" title="Standard Chinese">standard modern dialect</a>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Outer space</dt></dl>\n<p>Asteroid&#160;(239200)&#160;2006&#160;MD13 is named after Luoyang.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a text">&#27827;&#21335;&#31185;&#25216;&#22823;&#23398;</span>)</span></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luoyang_Normal_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luoyang Normal University (page does not exist)">Luoyang Normal University</a> <span class="nowrap">(<span lang="zh" title="Chinese language text">&#27931;&#38451;&#24072;&#33539;&#23398;&#38498;</span>)</span></li>\n<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=PLA_Foreign_Language_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="PLA Foreign class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col"><div id="Notes" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="font-size:85%;">Notes</span></div></th></tr><tr><td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">* Indicates this city has already occurred above.<br/>\n<p><sup>a</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-controlled_municipality_of_China" title="Direct-controlled municipality of China">Direct-controlled Municipalities</a>.\n<sup>b</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People\'s Republic of China">Sub-provincial cities as provincial capitals</a>.\n<sup>c</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-provincial_city_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Sub-provincial city in the People\'s Republic of China">Separate state-planning cities</a>.\n<sup>1</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Special Economic Zone Cities</a>.\n<sup>2</sup><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Economic_Zones_of_China" title="Special Economic Zones of China">Coastal development cities</a>.<br/>\n<sup>3</sup>Prefecture capital status established by Heilongjiang Province and not recognized by Ministry of Civil Affairs. Disputed by <a href="/wiki/Oroqen_Autonomous_Banner" title="Oroqen Autonomous Banner">Oroqen Autonomous Banner</a>, Hulunbuir, Inner Mongolia as part of it.<br/>\n<sup>4</sup>Only administers islands and waters in South China Sea and have no urban core comparable to typical cities in China.<br/>\n<sup>5</sup>The claimed province of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Province,_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Taiwan Province, People\'s Republic of China">Taiwan</a> no longer have any internal division announced by Ministry of Civil Affairs of PRC, due to lack of actual jurisdiction. of the Republic of China</a> instead.<br/>\n</p>\nAll provincial capitals are listed first in prefecture-level cities by
